            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-32 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-32">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>1.9 &#8212; Header files</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on June 3rd, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p><strong>Headers, and their purpose</strong></p>
<p>As programs grow larger and larger (and include more files), it becomes increasingly tedious to have to forward declare every function you want to use that lives in a different file.  Wouldn&#8217;t it be nice if you could put all your declarations in one place?</p>
<p>C++ code files (with a .cpp extension) are not the only files commonly seen in C++ programs.  The other type of file is called a <strong>header file</strong>, sometimes known as an <strong>include file</strong>.  Header files usually have a .h extension, but you will sometimes see them with a .hpp extension or no extension at all.  The purpose of a header file is to hold declarations for other files to use.</p>
<p><strong>Using standard library header files</strong></p>
<p>Consider the following program:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73461fdad538722094" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This program prints &#8220;Hello, world!&#8221; to the console using cout.  However, this program never defines cout, so how does the compiler know what cout is?  The answer is that cout has been declared in a header file called &#8220;iostream&#8221;.  When we use the line <code>#include &lt;iostream&gt;</code>, we&#8217;re requesting that all of the content from the header file named &#8220;iostream&#8221; be copied into the including file.  That makes the content from the header file available for use in our code file.</p>
<p>Keep in mind that header files typically only contain declarations.  They do not define how something is <em>implemented</em>.  So if cout is only <em>declared</em> in the &#8220;iostream&#8221; header file, where is it actually defined?  It is implemented in the C++ runtime support library, which is automatically linked into your program during the link phase.</p>
<p><img src="http://www.learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section1/IncludeLibrary.png"></p>
<p>Consider what would happen if the iostream header did not exist.  Wherever you used std::cout, you would have to manually copy in all of the declarations related to std::cout into the top of each file that used it!  This would require knowledge of what&#8217;s relevant and what&#8217;s not.  It&#8217;s much easier to just #include iostream!</p>
<p><strong>Writing your own header files</strong></p>
<p>Now let&#8217;s go back to the example we were discussing in the previous lesson.  When we left off, we had two files, add.cpp and main.cpp, that looked like this:</p>

<p></p>
<p>We&#8217;d used a forward declaration so that the compiler would know what add was when compiling main.cpp.  As previously mentioned, writing forward declarations for every function you want to use that lives in another file can get tedious quickly.</p>
<p>Header files can relieve us of this burden.  A header file only has to be written once, and it can be included in as many files as needed.  This also helps with maintenance by minimizing the number of changes that need to be made if a function prototype ever changes (eg. by adding a new parameter).</p>
<p>Writing our own header files is surprisingly easy.  Header files consist of two parts.</p>
<p>The first part is called a <strong>header guard</strong>, which is discussed in the next lesson (on the <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/110-a-first-look-at-the-preprocessor/">preprocessor</a>).  Header guards prevent a given header file from being #included more than once from the same file.</p>
<p>The second part is the actual content of the .h file, which should be the declarations for all of the functions we want other files to be able to see.  Our header files should all have a .h extension, so we&#8217;ll call our new header file add.h:</p>
<p>add.h:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In order to use this header file in main.cpp, we have to include it.</p>
<p>main.cpp that includes add.h:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div id="crayon-555d73461fdd5604393239-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">using</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">namespace</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fdd5604393239-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"The sum of 3 and 4 is "</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-cn">3</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73461fdd5604393239-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fdd5604393239-9"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>add.cpp stays the same:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73461fddc681397373-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When the compiler compiles the <code>#include &quot;add.h&quot;</code> line, it copies the contents of add.h into the current file at that point.  Because our add.h contains a function prototype for add(), this prototype is now being used as a forward declaration of add()!</p>
<p>Consequently, our program will compile and link correctly.</p>
<p><em>Note: When you #include a file, the entire content of the included file is inserted at the point of inclusion.</em></p>
<p><img src="http://www.learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section1/IncludeHeader.png"></p>
<p>If you get a compiler error about add.h not being found, make sure the file is really named add.h.  Depending on how you created and named it, it&#8217;s possible the file could have been named something like &#8220;add&#8221; (no extension) or &#8220;add.h.txt&#8221; or &#8220;add.hpp&#8221;.</p>
<p>If you get a linker error about add() not being defined, make sure you&#8217;ve included add.cpp in your project so it compiles properly!</p>
<p><strong>Angled brackets vs quotes</strong></p>
<p>You&#8217;re probably curious why we use angled brackets for iostream, and double quotes for add.h.  The answer is that angled brackets are used to tell the compiler that we are including a header file that was included with the compiler, so it should look for that header file in the system directories.  The double-quotes tell the compiler that this is a header file we are supplying, so it should look for that header file in the current directory containing our source code first.  If it doesn&#8217;t find the header file there, it will check any other include paths that you&#8217;ve specified as part of your compiler/IDE settings.  That failing, it will fall back to checking the system directories.</p>
<p><em>Rule: Use angled brackets to include header files that come with the compiler.  Use double quotes to include any other header files.</em></p>
<p><strong>Why doesn&#8217;t iostream have a .h extension?</strong></p>
<p>Another commonly asked question is &#8220;why doesn&#8217;t iostream (or any of the other standard library header files) have a .h extension?&#8221;.  The answer is, because iostream.h is a different header file than iostream is!  To explain requires a very short history lesson.</p>
<p>When C++ was first created, all of the files in the standard runtime library ended in .h.  Life was consistent, and it was good.  The original version of cout and cin lived in iostream.h.  When the language was standardized by the ANSI committee, they decided to move all of the functions in the runtime library into the std namespace (which is generally a good idea).  However, this presented a problem: if they moved all the functions into the std namespace, none of the old programs would work any more!</p>
<p>To try to get around this issue and provide backwards compatibility for older programs, a new set of header files was introduced that use the same names but lack the .h extension.  These new header files have all their functionality inside the std namespace.  This way, older programs that include <code>#include &lt;iostream.h&gt;</code> do not need to be rewritten, and newer programs can <code>#include &lt;iostream&gt;</code>.</p>
<p>When you include a header file from the standard library, make sure you use the non .h version if it exists.  Otherwise you will be using a deprecated version of the header that is no longer supported.</p>
<p>As a side note, many headers in the standard library do not have a non .h version, only a .h version.  For these files, it is fine to include the .h version.  Many of these libraries are backwards compatible with standard C programming, and C does not support namespaces.  Consequently, the functionality of these libraries will not be accessed through the std namespace.  Also, when you write your own header files, you should give them all a .h extension, since you will not be putting your code in the std namespace.</p>
<p><em>Rule: use the non .h version of a library if it exists, and access the functionality through the std namespace.  If the non .h version does not exist, or you are creating your own headers, use the .h version</em></p>
<p><strong>Including header files from other directories</strong></p>
<p>Another common question involves how to include header files from other directories.</p>
<p>One (bad) way to do this is to include a relative path to the header file you want to include as part of the #include line.  For example:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73461fde7057605245" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fde7057605245-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fde7057605245-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fde7057605245-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include "headers/myHeader.h"</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73461fde7057605245-2"><span class="crayon-p">#include "../moreHeaders/myOtherHeader.h"</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The downside of this approach is that it requires you to reflect your directory structure in your code.  If you ever update your directory structure, you code won&#8217;t work any more.</p>
<p>A better method is to tell your compiler or IDE that you have a bunch of header files in some other location, so that it will look there when it can&#8217;t find them in the current directory.  This can generally be done by setting an &#8220;include path&#8221; or &#8220;search directory&#8221; in your IDE project settings.</p>
<p>In Visual Studio, you can right click on your project in the Solution Explorer, and choose &#8220;Properties&#8221;, then the &#8220;VC++ Directories&#8221; tab.  From here, you will see a line called &#8220;Include Directories&#8221;.  Add your include directories there.</p>
<p>In Code::Blocks, go to the Project menu and select &#8220;Build Options&#8221;, then the &#8220;Search directories&#8221; tab.  Add your include directories there.</p>
<p>Using g++, you can use the -I option to specify an alternate include directory.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73461fdee788967222" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73461fdee788967222-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73461fdee788967222-1"><span class="crayon-v">g</span><span class="crayon-o">++</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">-</span><span class="crayon-i">o</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">main</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">-</span><span class="crayon-v">I</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">/</span><span class="crayon-v">source</span><span class="crayon-o">/</span><span class="crayon-e">includes </span><span class="crayon-v">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">cpp</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The nice thing about this approach is that if you ever change your directory structure, you only have to change a single compiler or IDE setting instead of every code file.</p>
<p><strong>Can I put function definitions in a header file?</strong></p>
<p>C++ won&#8217;t complain if you do, but generally speaking, you shouldn&#8217;t.</p>
<p>As noted above, when you #include a file, the entire content of the included file is inserted at the point of inclusion.  This means that any definitions you put in your header get copied into <em>every</em> file that includes that header.</p>
<p>For small projects, this isn&#8217;t likely to be much of an issue.  But for larger projects, this can make things take much longer to compile (as the same code gets recompiled each time it is encountered) and could significantly bloat the size of your executable.  If you make a change to a definition in a code file, only that .cpp file needs to be recompiled.  If you make a change to a definition in a header file, every code file that includes the header needs to be recompiled.  One small change can cause you to have to recompile your entire project!</p>
<p>Sometimes exceptions are made for trivial functions that are unlikely to change (e.g. where the function definition is one line).</p>
<p><strong>Header file best practices</strong></p>
<p>Here are a few best practices for creating your own header files.</p>
<ul>
<li>Always include header guards.</li>
<li>Do not define variables in header files unless they are constants.  Header files should generally only be used for declarations.</li>
<li>Do not define functions in header files.</li>
<li>Each header file should have a specific job, and be as independent as possible.  For example, you might put all your declarations related to functionality A in A.h and all your declarations related to functionality B in B.h.  That way if you only care about A later, you can just include A.h and not get any of the stuff related to B.
<li>Give your header files the same name as the source files they&#8217;re associated with (e.g. grades.h goes with grades.cpp).
<li>Try to minimize the number of other header files you #include in your header files.  Only #include what is necessary.</li>
<li>Do not #include .cpp files.</li>
</ul>

		<p>First of all thank you Alex for the excellent tutorials.</p>
<p>a questions please:</p>
<p>from jestuart&#8217;s code; I thought he will at least need three files, one for the header, one for the actual function and then one for main e.g<br />
Math.h - which contains the forward declaration<br />
Math.cpp - which will contain the actual function definition<br />
main.cpp - which will reference the .h files</p>
<p>here is my code for a similar operation; using code::block</p>
<p>main.cpp</p>
<p>#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;math.h&quot;</p>
<p> int main()<br />
 {<br />
     using namespace std;<br />
     cout &lt;&lt; &quot;3 + 4 = &quot; &lt;&lt; add(3, 4) &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
     cout &lt;&lt; &quot;3 - 4 = &quot; &lt;&lt; sub(3, 4) &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
     cout &lt;&lt; &quot;3 * 4 = &quot; &lt;&lt; multiply(3, 4) &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
     return 0;<br />
 }</p>
<p>math.cpp</p>
<p>int add( int x, int y)<br />
{<br />
    return x + y;<br />
}</p>
<p>int sub(int x, int y)<br />
{<br />
    return x - y;<br />
}</p>
<p>int multiply(int x, int y)<br />
{<br />
    return x * y;<br />
}</p>
<p>math.h</p>
<p>#ifndef MATH_H<br />
#define MATH_H</p>
<p>int add(int x, int y);<br />
int sub(int x, int y);<br />
int multiply(int x, int y);</p>
<p>#endif</p>
		</div>

<p>the following is the final code for the header (math.h) file:</p>

		<div id="crayon-555d734626049707935313" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251329">
		February 2, 2015 at 5:43 pm</a>
        		 
		</div>
		<p>It is bad form to #include .cpp files.</p>
<p>It sounds to me like in this case, math.cpp wasn&#8217;t being compiled in the project.  So instead, you have main.cpp #include math.h, which #includes math.cpp.  This means the code from math.h and math.cpp get inserted into main.cpp.  That defeats much of the point of having separate files.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-10090">
		<div id="div-comment-10090" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-10090">
		March 21, 2008 at 10:12 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=10090#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-10090", "10090", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>As you&#8217;ve noted, the header guards prevent the header files from being included multiple times.  It&#8217;s a sloppy way of doing things, in my opinion, but it works and it&#8217;s the standard way to do it.</p>
<p>Ideally, you should include your header file in every .cpp file in which you use the stuff it declares.  However, in practice, since header files can include other header files, this may not be strictly necessary.  For example, you might have a class named Foo that uses strings, so foo.h will include string.h.  foo.cpp (which also uses strings) should ideally include both foo.h and string.h, but since foo.h already includes string.h, if you only include foo.h you will still be able to use strings.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<li class="comment even depth-3 clearfix" id="comment-62965">
		<div id="div-comment-62965" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/7b761092fa0823d599a228b787ee5a78?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/7b761092fa0823d599a228b787ee5a78?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">TBM</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-62965">
		June 23, 2009 at 5:40 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=62965#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-62965", "62965", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to TBM'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The problem Chase had here as do to the omission of the semi colon &#8221; ; &#8221; after his prototype for his header file and the reason it was fixed when he changed it was simply do to the fact that he defined it within the header itself instead of in a separate .cpp file.</p>
<p>In other words his declaration should have looked like this in his header file:</p>
<p>add(int x, int y); &lt;-- notice the semi colon.</p>
<p>When changed to:</p>
<p>add(int x, int y)<br />
{<br />
   return x + y;<br />
}</p>
<p>It was no longer a prototype but a definition, meaning that the add.cpp file was no longer needed do to the fact that the definition is also now held in the header file. At least this is my understanding so far.</p>
<p>Oh, and yes I know his change uses a colon instead of a semi colon, I&#8217;m just guessing that it was a typo.</p>
		</div>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-27035">
		<div id="div-comment-27035" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-27035">
		September 10, 2008 at 10:47 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=27035#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-27035", "27035", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When main.cpp #includes add.h, the function prototype for add() is imported into main.cpp.  The compiler uses this add() prototype to ensure anyone calling add() is doing so correctly.</p>
<p>Once the compiler is satisfied no syntax or type-checking errors exist, the linker takes over.  The linker&#8217;s job is to combine all of the individual .cpp files into a single unit (generally an executable or DLL), and ensure that all of the function calls resolve to an actual defined function.</p>
<p>If you forgot to include add.cpp in your project, your project would still compile okay (because the compiler could use the prototype to do type checking), but it would fail in the linker stage because the linker would be unable to resolve the call to add() to a specific function.</p>
		</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=34521#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-34521", "34521", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It looks to me like the linker can&#8217;t resolve the function call to add(), which means that you&#8217;re probably not compiling in add.cc properly.  If I remember correctly, you should be doing something like this:</p>
<p>c++ main.cc add.cc -o out.exe</p>
		</div>

<p>So the compiling syntax is:</p>
<p>C++ mainfile.cc Inclue1.cc Include2.cc &#8230; IncludeN.cc -o out.exe</p>
<p>where InlcudeN are the N additional header files to be read in mainfile.</p>
<p>Is that a generic compiling syntax, or is this just specific to Cygwin???</p>

		</div>
		<p>If you&#8217;re using a MS compiler, on the left hand side you should see your project and a list of all the files include in it.  If you right click on &#8220;Source Files&#8221; and choose &#8220;add&#8221; you can add new files or existing files to your project.  That&#8217;s where you need to add the file.</p>
<p>Using #include with .cpp is almost never something you&#8217;ll have need of.</p>

		<p>excellent tutorials(thank you!) but I have 3 questions.</p>
<p>I don&#8217;t get the header file part.<br />
In the example you use add.cpp as the declaration for add(). In add.h you put in a forward declaration for add(). But why can&#8217;t you define add() in the header file, isn&#8217;t that more efficient since you don&#8217;t need add.cpp anymore and thus less files = less work.</p>
<p>Second question (assuming you answered my first question):<br />
You use add.cpp as a declaration file for add(), is it common to use a .cpp file with more then one declarations? Meaning multiple function declarations in one .cpp file (seems more convenient) or do you have to use multiple cpp files for multiple function declarations?</p>
<p>My last question:</p>
<p>Will these tutorials lead to the explaination of actually using your knowledge of c++ in developing programs? I think that&#8217;s really important because: okay I learned c++, now how do I use my knowledge? Like this tutorial gives you an assignment to make a program in the end.</p>
<p>Many thanks, keep it up!</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-42012">
		<div id="div-comment-42012" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-42012">
		February 6, 2009 at 12:26 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=42012#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-42012", "42012", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You _could_ define add() in the header file if you wanted, but this is generally not done (unless the function is trivial, like 1 or 2 statements).  Header files are generally used for prototyping functions and declaring classes, and then those things are actually implemented in .cpp files.</p>
<p>It is VERY common to have multiple functions in one .cpp file.  Typically a .cpp file will contain a whole set of related function (eg. math.cpp will contain functions to do square roots, exponents, and other mathy things).</p>
<p>To address your last question, no, not really.  It&#8217;s really up to you to figure out how to apply what you learn.  At some point I&#8217;d love to go back and add that, but I haven&#8217;t had time. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/frownie.png" alt=":(" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-58904">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=58904#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-58904", "58904", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to csvan'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It is always a good idea to go over good, rich materials twice. I believe that the things you learn later on (not specifically in this tutorial, but anything) will help you better understand the basics when you go over them again. Generally, as you build a programmer mindset and learn to think, reason and think accordingly, I believe you will also find it easier to put things into perspective, so you might finally understand basic things you never understood the first thing you saw them.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=47826#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-47826", "47826", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Justin'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>How do i create a header in Dev C++? your help would be appreciated</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-78619">
		<div id="div-comment-78619" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/485576a3e34f44e6bd426eff518f5462?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/485576a3e34f44e6bd426eff518f5462?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Tyler</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-78619">
		February 19, 2010 at 1:20 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=78619#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-78619", "78619", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Tyler'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>In order to create a header file in dev-cpp, in the upper-left corrner there is a &#8216;new&#8217; button (button with a pic of a blank peice of paper on it), click on this. once the file is created, right click the filename in the left hand column, and select rename. Enter the new name for the file and put .h at the end of the name. This will state it as being a header file and thus cuase the linker to treat it as such.</p>
<p>-Tyler</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251346">
		<div id="div-comment-251346" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251346">
		February 3, 2015 at 3:46 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251346#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251346", "251346", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>In trivial examples like the ones we&#8217;re doing right now, there&#8217;s really no need for header files.</p>
<p>However, once you get into writing more complicated things, you&#8217;ll use header files everywhere.  They allow you to import a set of declarations to multiple source (.cpp) files with minimal effort.</p>
<p>An analogy might be useful here: imagine every time you wanted to use std::cout, you had to copy every thing related to std::cout into the top of your .cpp.  For every .cpp file.  That would get annoying, right?  Isn&#8217;t it much easier to just #include <iostream>?</iostream></p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

				</table>
			</div>
		</div>

<p></p>
<p>I get the error &#8220;add(int, int)&#8221; not defined</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251348">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251348#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251348", "251348", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I&#8217;m not sure why this is working for you.  ADD_H should be meaningless.</p>
<p>The header guard ensures that the header is not included more than once (that would lead to redefinition errors).</p>
<p>You are allowed to have more than one function prototype in a header file.</p>
		</div>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-79688">
		March 4, 2010 at 8:26 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=79688#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-79688", "79688", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Shaun'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I actually figured it out. It appears that within project explorer, you can right click the file and select properties. It&#8217;s important to make sure that under the Build tab, the Debug and Release boxes are checked. Apparently, when I created the file I missed the step to check these boxes. All compiles as expected now.</p>

		<p>For those of you who are using Visual Studio and are getting errors. This will fix it!!</p>
<p>First off you don&#8217;t need add.cpp, because add.h is your&#8221;library for the function&#8221;<br />
-If you are following along with the tutorial you need to edit the add.h file.<br />
-It needs to be as follows:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d734625988912504196" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d734625988912504196-10">10</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-1"><span class="crayon-p">#ifndef ADD_H</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-p">#define ADD_H</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-3">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// function prototype for add.h</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">// without this the function doesn't know what you want it to do</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-8">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-9">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d734625988912504196-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-p">#endif</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0011 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Reason for the change&#8230;a function must be declared in order to work.</p>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-3 clearfix" id="comment-251350">
		<div id="div-comment-251350" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251350">
		February 3, 2015 at 4:56 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251350#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251350", "251350", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>This works, but I generally wouldn&#8217;t advise it.</p>
<p>If you define your function in the header file, then the full definition of that function will be copied into EVERY file that includes it.  For trivial functions that may not be much of an issue, but for larger files this can bloat the size of your code significantly.</p>
<p>The root of your problem is likely that you didn&#8217;t include add.cpp in your project file.  Fix that and you don&#8217;t need to define the add() function in the header.</p>
		</div>

		<p>Thanx Alex you are certainly a king amongst men, and patient with us newbies. Because I was forever #including the other .cpp in the main.cpp and getting a linker error. It kept saying I had declared a function twice: in the header file and main.cpp!</p>
<p>In desperation, sometimes I did not include the header file in the main.cpp, in hope it would compile and link. I read your tut twice and began looking through my code and then realised I was declaring it twice, when I #included the other.cpp in which the offending function was declared, in the main.cpp where it was called.</p>
<p>My bad. Thanx for a great tutorial.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251353#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251353", "251353", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The linker is complaining it can&#8217;t find a definition for function add().  Odds are you either forgot to include add.cpp in your project (even though it&#8217;s in the right directory), or it&#8217;s not compiling/linking for some reason (check your project settings and make sure the file isn&#8217;t being excluded from compilation)</p>

		February 3, 2015 at 5:14 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251356#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251356", "251356", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>> In header add.h, add() is not defined</p>
<p>That&#8217;s intentional.  In header files, we typically only declare functions, not define them.</p>
<p>Add.cpp defines the add() function.  Most people who are having problems aren&#8217;t including add.cpp in their projects, so the definition of add() is not being linked into their programs.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-207938">
		<div id="div-comment-207938" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2dc58df301aaf9474e1d1a1a14608917?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2dc58df301aaf9474e1d1a1a14608917?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">rameye</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-207938">
		November 2, 2014 at 2:29 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=207938#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-207938", "207938", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to rameye'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You are correct, header files are for containing forward declarations to things that exist outside of your .cpp file.</p>
<p>However, what if the forward declarations in the header file also make reference to outside things? Perhaps the forward declaration&#8217;s return type, or it&#8217;s parameter types, need also to have their own forward declarations.</p>
<p>This is why a .h header file would include more header files, to bring in those forward declarations of things referenced in it&#8217;s own forward declarations.</p>
<p>Also a header file may make use of constants, and those constants may be declared in another header file that must be included.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-3 clearfix" id="comment-251357">
		<div id="div-comment-251357" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251357">
		February 3, 2015 at 5:25 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251357#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251357", "251357", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>This is correct.  It&#8217;s not uncommon for header files to include other header files that contain things they need.</p>
<p>For example, lets say you have a function prototype that looks like this:</p>
<p>std::string sayHi();</p>
<p>How does the compiler know what std::string is?  This header will have to include &lt;string&gt;</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<p>Where is your add.cpp file? Did you create it and add it to the project? If not it will not be compiled during the build and then the linker will not find the add function, thus the &#8220;undefined reference&#8221; error.</p>

		February 23, 2013 at 6:06 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=98200#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-98200", "98200", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to gu_obos'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>As an FYI to anyone else having issues with Visual Studio 2012 and having issues with with building:</p>
<p>If precompiled headers are turned on, you *must* have #include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221; as the first include. Otherwise your includes don&#8217;t work.</p>
<p>See this link for more info:<br />
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precompiled_header#stdafx.h</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-102796">
		<div id="div-comment-102796" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/21b2deaaa0bcf172aa88051b6cf7ba1f?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/21b2deaaa0bcf172aa88051b6cf7ba1f?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://127.0.0.1/' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>zingmars</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-102796">
		August 19, 2013 at 5:32 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=102796#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-102796", "102796", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to zingmars'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Why use header files - When you have 10k or more lines of code having it in one file is a royal pain. You use header files to split code between multiple files helping in both project management and code readability.<br />
Why is the standard library precompiled - The standard libs are large. Thousands of lines of code large. You do not want to recompile it every time you want to see whether your program works. That&#8217;s why they&#8217;re precompiled.<br />
Why standard header files don&#8217;t have the .h extension - some do. .h extension is useless and only wastes your time when you have to write it.</p>
		</div>

		September 13, 2013 at 2:44 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=104527#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-104527", "104527", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to lilith'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Ok, I&#8217;ve solved my problem myself. It didn&#8217;t have anything to do with the example code, but simply with my lack of knowledge of g++.</p>
<p>For any of you running into the same problem:<br />
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%<br />
g++ -c main.cpp<br />
g++ -c Complex.cpp<br />
g++ main.o Complex.o<br />
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%<br />
This does the trick. Next, if you check the contents of your source file, you see an  executable named &#8220;a.out&#8221;, which you have to call (&#8220;./a.out&#8221;) to run your code.<br />
Everything peachy now, I finally can move on with this very helpful tutorial!</p>
		</div>

<p><strong> main.cpp </strong><br />
<code><br />
#include<br />
#include "main.h"</p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>

{<br />
	int uservalue=0;<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;enter a value:&quot; &lt;&gt; uservalue;<br />

}<br />
</code></p>
<p><strong> main.h </strong><br />
<code></p>

{<br />
	return x * 2;<br />
}<br />

		<p>I just updated the tutorial to cover this topic, because it&#8217;s one that gets asked fairly often.</p>
<p>In short, while it&#8217;s something you can do, you generally shouldn&#8217;t, because it&#8217;ll increase your compile times and bloat the size of your executable.</p>

		</div>
		<p>Just in case anybody else runs into the problem, if you&#8217;re using Visual Studio with precompiled headers turned on (which they are by default), you need to #include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221; at the top of all your code files, otherwise Visual Studio complains.</p>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251688">
		March 1, 2015 at 8:10 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251688#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251688", "251688", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Josh'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Follow description maybe incorrect, as far as I known, read/load all the file context from header file stuff should be done by c++ preprocessor, but not compiler. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /> </p>
<p>When we use the line #include &lt;iostream&gt;, we are telling the compiler to locate and then read all the declarations from a header file named iostream.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251697">
		<div id="div-comment-251697" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">

		</div>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-251697">
		March 2, 2015 at 5:54 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=251697#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251697", "251697", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You are correct, it is the preprocessor that includes all of the content from the header file.</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve updated the wording in this section to be more agnostic of how #include works, since I don&#8217;t introduce the preprocessor formally until the next section, where it&#8217;s discussed in more detail.</p>

<p>Then here is my source file getX.cpp</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73462448d805095656" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

					<tr class="crayon-row">

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-3 clearfix" id="comment-252048">

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-252048">
		April 3, 2015 at 9:36 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252048#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252048", "252048", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Very close.  Iostream.h contains the declaration for cout, which is inside the std namespace.  The <em>definition</em> of cout lives in the C++ runtime library, which is linked into your program when you compile it.</p>
		</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252094#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252094", "252094", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>If you want to know what&#8217;s in the std namespace, you&#8217;re probably best off looking at external documentation.</p>
<p>By viewing the header files that are part of the standard library (e.g. iostream), you can see all of the declarations that are part of the std namespace.  But those files tend to be complicated, so don&#8217;t be surprised if they&#8217;re basically unintelligible. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>

		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/607c9eb2a63c36df30aca447bf2c652a?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/607c9eb2a63c36df30aca447bf2c652a?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Daniel W</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-252216">
		April 22, 2015 at 10:37 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252216#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252216", "252216", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Daniel W'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>this one works:<br />
==============================<br />
Create Interface Cat.h<br />
==============================<br />
#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;</p>
<p>class Cat<br />
{</p>
<p>private:<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int GetAge();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;void SetAge(int age);<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;void Meow();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;void Bark();</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp; };<br />
========================<br />
Create Cat Implementation CatImpl.cpp<br />
=======================<br />
#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;<br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;Cat.h&quot;</p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>class CatImpl{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;public:<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unsigned int Age;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unsigned int Weight;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int itsAge;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;CatImpl::CatImpl(int initialAge)// constructor of Cat,<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Age = initialAge;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; }<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;CatImpl::~CatImpl()<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;{ }// destructor, takes no action<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;int CatImpl::GetAge()// public accessors<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; return Age;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;}<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; void CatImpl::SetAge(int age)<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;{<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Age = age;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;}<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; void CatImpl::Meow(){<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; cout&lt;&lt;&quot;This cat Meown&quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;}&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;// private member data<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;void CatImpl::Bark(){<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; cout&lt;&lt;&quot;This cat BARKn&quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;}</p>
<p>};<br />
==========================<br />
Create Main Class SimpleClass.cpp<br />
===================================<br />
// SimpleClass.cpp : main project file.<br />
#include &quot;stdafx.h&quot;<br />
#include &lt;iostream&gt;<br />
#include &quot;CatImpl.cpp&quot;</p>
<p>//using namespace System;<br />
using namespace std;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
int main()<br />
{<br />
int x;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; CatImpl Frisky(50);<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp; // Frisky.SetAge(5); // assign to the member variable<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Frisky is a cat who is &quot; ;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;x=Frisky.GetAge();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; x&lt;&lt; &quot; years old.n&quot;;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Frisky.Meow();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Frisky.Bark();<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cout &lt;&lt; x&lt;&lt; &quot; years old.n&quot;;<br />
Frisky.SetAge(25);<br />
x=Frisky.GetAge();<br />
cout &lt;&lt; x&lt;&lt; &quot; New Age.n&quot;;<br />
cout &lt;&lt; &quot;n&quot;;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
system(&quot;PAUSE&quot;);<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return 0;<br />
}</p>
		</div>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-252476">
		May 15, 2015 at 3:00 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252476#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252476", "252476", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The function definition lives in a .cpp file.  When your programs are small, this will be whatever you named your main .cpp file.  As your program gets larger, you&#8217;ll probably want to have matched pairs of .cpp and .h files (e.g. all your math functions go in math.cpp and the associated declarations in math.h).</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-4 clearfix" id="comment-252526">
		<div id="div-comment-252526" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-252526">

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252526#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252526", "252526", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You got it.  When you #include add.h, it&#8217;ll bring the forward declaration for the function declared in add.h into the current file, allowing you to use the function.</p>
<p>This method is super useful when you have a function or set of functions that you need to use in a lot of places.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252494#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252494", "252494", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Humphrey'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When you use a forward declaration to alert the compiler of a function not yet defined, while there is a function in another file with the same name but different definition due to the limited visibility in each file, what is the result?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252508">
		<div id="div-comment-252508" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/#comment-252508">
		May 18, 2015 at 4:11 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/19-header-files/?replytocom=252508#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252508", "252508", "respond", "32" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The forward declaration actually doesn&#8217;t matter in this example.</p>
<p>If the two functions are declared in different files and neither function has visibility beyond that file, then the program should still compile.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
	
	</ul>
	<!-- / Comment List -->
